    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }

<div id="descriptionContainer">
  
      <div id="description" class="readable stacked" style="right:0">
        
<span id="freeTextContainer5510487319547683236">Twelve-year-old September lives in Omaha, and used to have an ordinary life, until her father went to war and her mother went to work. One day, September is met at her kitchen window by a Green Wind (taking the form of a gentleman in a green jacket), who invites her on an adventure, implying that her help is needed in Fairyland. The new Marquess is unpredictable and fickle</span>
  <span id="freeText5510487319547683236" style="display:none">Twelve-year-old September lives in Omaha, and used to have an ordinary life, until her father went to war and her mother went to work. One day, September is met at her kitchen window by a Green Wind (taking the form of a gentleman in a green jacket), who invites her on an adventure, implying that her help is needed in Fairyland. The new Marquess is unpredictable and fickle, and also not much older than September. Only September can retrieve a talisman the Marquess wants from the enchanted woods, and if she doesn’t . . . then the Marquess will make life impossible for the inhabitants of Fairyland. September is already making new friends, including a book-loving Wyvern and a mysterious boy named Saturday. <div> </div><div>With exquisite illustrations by acclaimed artist Ana Juan, <i>Fairyland </i>lives up to the sensation it created when the author first posted it online. For readers of all ages who love the charm of <i>Alice in Wonderland</i> and the soul of <i>The Golden Compass</i>, here is a reading experience unto itself: unforgettable, and so very beautiful.</div><div></div></span>
  <a data-text-id="5510487319547683236" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

      </div>

<div class='questionText'>
<a href="/questions/383647-hey-all-i-would-appreciate-your">Hey all, I would appreciate your advice.

I just finished the first book and it left me in a state of wonder. I know (after reading more) that the author has followed up with all kinds of things ... .05 and such.

My question: I&#39;ve only read the first book. What should I read now so as not to taint that experience?

Thanks, community.</a>
</div>

<div class='allCommunityAnswers'>
<div class='communityAnswer'>
<div class='communityAnswerBody'>
<div class='answererUserIcon'>
<a class="leftAlignedImage userPhoto" href="/user/show/63761241-morgan-nikola-wren"><img alt="" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/users/1544923705i/63761241._UX100_CR0,0,100,100_.jpg" /></a>
</div>
<div class='communityAnswerTextContainer'>
<span class='communityAnswererName'>
<a href="/user/show/63761241-morgan-nikola-wren">Morgan Nikola-Wren</a>
</span>
<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">Hey Christina, <br/><br/>As someone who fell so hard for the first book that I have a tattoo referencing it on my foot, I felt honor-bound to answer this questi<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">Hey Christina, <br /><br />As someone who fell so hard for the first book that I have a tattoo referencing it on my foot, I felt honor-bound to answer this question. ;)<br /><br />I found myself utterly and beautifully lost in all the rest of the books in the Fairyland series. Granted, I too, was worried that the sequels could not live up to the olden standard the first set for me, but as soon as I opened the second book and found myself greeted by the lemony narrator, I felt like I had been reunited with an old friend. The following four books serve to expound upon so many of the themes introduced in the original. And the short story prequel, The Girl Who Ruled Fairyland...But Only for a Little While, had me crying at the end, and then reading it aloud to my husband, because he just needed to know the story that badly. Also, if it's worth anything, I often don't finish all the books in a series. (No. Not even Narnia.) I'll like the first and maybe the next well enough, but I often get the feeling that the author is stretching things too far and my interest gets lost. So, I think that should count for something. <br /><br />Hope this is helpful...Though, I just looked and saw you posted this question two years ago. <br /><br />Morgan<br /><br />PS: If you're still looking for additional, arresting reading material with a fairy tale lean, I loved Neil Gaiman's The Ocean at the End of the Lane so much that I took it to a wedding...and spent most of the reception reading it.<br /><br />PPS: The tattoo is the glass orb with a leaf in it that The Green Wind gives to September. Because, my gosh, THAT WELL SCENE!<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>
</div>

<div id="review_1032730773" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1032730773" />
    <a title="Patrick" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/922495-patrick"><img alt="Patrick" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1351307095p2/922495.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1032730773?book_show_action=true">Aug 21, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Patrick" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Patrick" href="/user/show/922495-patrick">Patrick</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/922495-patrick?shelf=good-books-for-little-kids">good-books-for-little-kids</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/922495-patrick?shelf=books-i-would-blurb">books-i-would-blurb</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1032730773" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10077937623367696870">I walked into the bookstore in a bit of a mood. <br/><br/>Wait, that's my Midwestern nature talking. We tend to understate. The truth is I walked into the bookstore furious at the world. I can't remember why. I am prone to dark moods, and when I'm in the middle of one, I tend to rumble through the world like an angry old-testament god. <br/><br/>I went directly to the Sci-Fi Fantasy section. That's where I live for the most part. That's where I go when the world gets to be too much for me. <br/><br/>I looked at the titles. I</span>
  <span id="freeText10077937623367696870" style="display:none">I walked into the bookstore in a bit of a mood. <br /><br />Wait, that's my Midwestern nature talking. We tend to understate. The truth is I walked into the bookstore furious at the world. I can't remember why. I am prone to dark moods, and when I'm in the middle of one, I tend to rumble through the world like an angry old-testament god. <br /><br />I went directly to the Sci-Fi Fantasy section. That's where I live for the most part. That's where I go when the world gets to be too much for me. <br /><br />I looked at the titles. I'd read about a quarter of them. I read a lot. But nothing looked particularly good. Nothing does when I'm in one of my moods. <br /><br />A friendly bookseller walked over. "Can I help you find anything?" she asked. <br /><br />"I want to read something good," I said. "I'm tired of gritty depressing shit. I want a fun, light book that isn't going to leave me wanting to put a gun in my mouth." <br /><br />I'm not hyperbolizing. That's what I actually said. It wasn't a nice thing to say, but I can be unpleasantly brusk at times. <br /><br />The bookseller didn't bat and eye. She pointed out a couple books, then asked how I felt about YA. <br /><br />"I'll read anything if it's good," I said. <br /><br />She pointed out this book. I'd heard of it before, appreciated its awesome title. I like faerie stories. Most importantly, I've read Cat Valente's work before, and I know she has a marvelous grip on the language. <br /><br />Five pages into this book, I thought, "Why didn't I read this years ago? Why haven't I heard about this book before?" <br /><br />I flipped to the back cover and saw blurbs from Neil Gaiman and Peter S. Beagle. "Oh," I thought. "Probably because I'm an idiot who lives under a rock." <br /><br />Ten pages in, I was irritated. Fifteen pages in, I was jealous. Twenty pages in, I was in love. <br /><br />So. A review: <br /><br />This book is beautiful. The language is lovely without being pretentious. The story is careful and playful and smart. This book made me tear up in places. Not because it is particularly sad. But because sometimes when a story is true and sweet and perfectly shaped, it puts its hand around my heart. <br /><br />This book is everything I love about Victorian faerie tales without all the tedious bullshit. <br /><br />This is the best book I've read all year. And I read a *lot* of books. <br /><br />I look forward to reading this book to my little boy. And that, ultimately, is the best thing I can say about a book. <br /><br />So yeah. Read it. Read it ten times. </span>
  <a data-text-id="10077937623367696870" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_168539084" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/168539084" />
    <a title="Stephen" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1413439-stephen"><img alt="Stephen" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1311616811p2/1413439.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/168539084?book_show_action=true">May 15, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Stephen" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Stephen" href="/user/show/1413439-stephen">Stephen</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1413439-stephen?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1413439-stephen?shelf=ebooks">ebooks</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1413439-stephen?shelf=ya">ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1413439-stephen?shelf=humor-and-satire">humor-and-satire</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1413439-stephen?shelf=audiobook">audiobook</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1413439-stephen?shelf=2011">2011</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1413439-stephen?shelf=love-those-words">love-those-words</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1413439-stephen?shelf=6-star-books">6-star-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1413439-stephen?shelf=all-time-favorites">all-time-favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer168539084" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4351520165509224618"><b><u>WINNER</u>: BESTest, BRILLIANTest, most EXCELLENTest, YA Novel in HistorYA!!!</b><br/><a href='http://s153.photobucket.com/albums/s207/sullypython/Book%20covers/?action=view&current=GirlWhoCircumnavigatedFairyland-1.jpg' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380349939i/703874.jpg' alt='Photobucket' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/> <br/>I know, I know, that comes as a bit of a shocker, what with <i>Potter</i>, <i>Percy</i> and those <i>Hunger Gamers</i> running from all those <i>Sparkly Emos</i> and bumping into <i>Bartimaeus</i> hiding inside <i>His Dark Materials</i> waiting for some <i>Giver</i> of an <i>Abhorsen</i> to find their <i>Wrinkle in Time</i> to send them all back to <i>Wonderland</i>. Not to mention that AMAZO <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6171892.Genesis' title='Genesis by Bernard Beckett' rel='nofollow noopener'>Genesis</a> I read earlier this year (sorry I couldn't work it in above). <br/><br/>However, despite all of th</span>
  <span id="freeText4351520165509224618" style="display:none"><b><u>WINNER</u>: BESTest, BRILLIANTest, most EXCELLENTest, YA Novel in HistorYA!!!</b><br><a href="http://s153.photobucket.com/albums/s207/sullypython/Book%20covers/?action=view&amp;current=GirlWhoCircumnavigatedFairyland-1.jpg" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380349939i/703874.jpg" alt="Photobucket" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br> <br>I know, I know, that comes as a bit of a shocker, what with <i>Potter</i>, <i>Percy</i> and those <i>Hunger Gamers</i> running from all those <i>Sparkly Emos</i> and bumping into <i>Bartimaeus</i> hiding inside <i>His Dark Materials</i> waiting for some <i>Giver</i> of an <i>Abhorsen</i> to find their <i>Wrinkle in Time</i> to send them all back to <i>Wonderland</i>. Not to mention that AMAZO <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6171892.Genesis" title="Genesis by Bernard Beckett" rel="nofollow noopener">Genesis</a> I read earlier this year (sorry I couldn't work it in above). <br><br>However, despite all of those "mostly" special literary achievements, this story by Ms. Valente and her amazing protagonist September has more concentrated WUP (win units per page) than any other “too young to vote” fiction I have ever read. The writing, humor, plot, narrative voice, characters, imagination and respect for the reader that this gem of a book shows is something rare and very, very special. <br><br>As I look over my list of all time favorite books (of any genre), one element that seems to appear most often is unforgettable prose and a unique voice. From Mieville in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/68494.Perdido_Street_Station" title="Perdido Street Station by China Miéville" rel="nofollow noopener">Perdido Street Station</a>, to McCarthy in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/12497.No_Country_for_Old_Men" title="No Country for Old Men by Cormac McCarthy" rel="nofollow noopener">No Country for Old Men</a>, to Winslow in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/8008928.Savages" title="Savages by Don Winslow" rel="nofollow noopener">Savages</a> and to Gaiman in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/4407.American_Gods" title="American Gods by Neil Gaiman" rel="nofollow noopener">American Gods</a>, these writers get my pulse up and running and make my brain swell with jealousy and drip envy for the unworldly skills of these master wordsmiths.<br><br>Well folks, Ms. Valante will be buying the next round at the “We Write so Amazingly Well That We Make You Feel Stupid and Inadequate” pub session. The writing in this story is exquisite that it’s painful. It is descriptive and brilliant, yet humorous and whimsical. It is just flawless in what it tries to do...namely entertain, enlighten and bring a sense of wonder and joy. <br><br>Those of you that have read previously read Valente’s <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/202769.In_the_Night_Garden__The_Orphan_s_Tales___1_" title="In the Night Garden (The Orphan's Tales, #1) by Catherynne M. Valente" rel="nofollow noopener">In the Night Garden</a>, knows that she can pen prose like nobody’s business and tell a complex yet readable story with nuance and care. Here, she has taken that gift, brought it to the YA format and created a new standard in excellence that I hope many try to follow. <br><br>Let me take a quick babble gush break and give you a thumbnail of the plot. A young girl in Nebraska gets taken by the Green Wind and his companion, the Leopard of Little Breezes, to Fairyland for an unforgettable adventure. Along the way, she ends up meeting more fantastical people, creatures and places than you could shake a magic stick at without having said stick turn around look at you and tell you to knock it off. <br><br>Okay, that’s enough of the plot as you will be able to explore that creamy nuggety goodness all on your own. Let's get back to the writing. Here is a scene from the beginning of the book: <blockquote>
  <i> “How does one get to Fairyland? After a while, we shall certainly pass India and Japan and California and simply come round to my house again.”<br>The Green Wind chuckled. “I suppose that would be true if the earth were round.”<br>“I’m reasonably sure it is…”<br>“You’re going to have to stop that sort of backward, old-fashioned thinking, you know. Conservatism is not an attractive trait. Fairyland is a very Scientifick place. We subscribe to all the best journals.”<br>The Leopard of Little Breezes gave a light roar. Several small clouds skipped huffily out of their path.<br>“The earth, my dear is roughly trapezoidal, vaguely rhomboid, a bit of a tessaract, and altogether grumpy when its fur is stroked the wrong way! In short, it is a puzzle, my autumnal acquisition…”</i>
</blockquote> C'mon...just say Ahhhhhh!!!<br><br><br>In addition to the story itself, Ms. Valente does something I really love to see in stories like this that have “OMG so much is happening every second that it is hard to keep track of where we are going” plots. She gives the reader a map of what's coming without spoiling any of the story. For example, here is the heading for the second chapter in the book. <blockquote>CHAPTER II<br><b>THE CLOSET BETWEEN WORLDS</b><br><i>In which September Passes Between Worlds, asks Four Questions and Receives Twelve Answers, and Is Inspected by a Customs Officer</i>
</blockquote> Thus, we are given hints as to what to look for, but no way of knowing what it means until it happens and at which point we smile, say wow wow wubsy and bask in the warm and fuzzy glow of the awesomeness. <br><br>Oh, and a quick word on the ART. The art is terrific and is a perfect compliment to the story. For example: <br><a href="http://s153.photobucket.com/albums/s207/sullypython/Fantasy%20SF%20Art/?action=view&amp;current=Fairyland1__V180501125_.jpg" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380349939i/703875.jpg" alt="Photobucket" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Just another aspect of this incredible read. <br><br>Before I wrap this up, I want to pay one final compliment to Ms. Valente (and also to other writers who show great respect for their readers). While this is a story that I think YAs will love, I believe that it is the adults, especially those of us that love lush language and witty words, that will enjoy this the most. This is because Ms. Valente doesn’t dumb down her story AT ALL. This is a YA book written as much for adults as for YAs (kind of like the movie Shrek with all the little "adult" in jokes). <br>The story has a way of making you feel like a younger version of yourself as you read it. <br>The story is sometimes dark, but always beautiful. There is adventure, pain, bravery, lessons about life and growing up, magic, hardship, sadness, mysteries, laughter, amazing characters and OH, THE WRITING. Buy this book...read the book....love the book...re-read this book. 6.0 Stars HIGHEST POSSIBLE RECOMMENDATION!!<br><br>P.S. I listened to the audio version read by the author and she was absolutely amazing...I mean amazing. If you have a chance to experience it..DO!! <br><br></span>
  <a data-text-id="4351520165509224618" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<tr class="no_border feedFooterReview" id="update_comment_stuff_Review168539084">

<div id="review_296609396" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/296609396" />
    <a title="Nataliya" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3672777-nataliya"><img alt="Nataliya" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1605995014p2/3672777.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/296609396?book_show_action=true">Mar 18, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nataliya" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nataliya" href="/user/show/3672777-nataliya">Nataliya</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">People who like intelligent YA fantasy</span></div>

          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Nataliya by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/1886642-catie">Catie</a>
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3672777-nataliya?shelf=valente-whimsical-magic">valente-whimsical-magic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3672777-nataliya?shelf=2012-reads">2012-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3672777-nataliya?shelf=locus-winner">locus-winner</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3672777-nataliya?shelf=lodestar-and-andre-norton-awards">lodestar-and-andre-norton-awards</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3672777-nataliya?shelf=location-is-the-true-protagonist">location-is-the-true-protagonist</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3672777-nataliya?shelf=awesome-kickass-heroines">awesome-kickass-heroines</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3672777-nataliya?shelf=for-my-future-hypothetical-daughter">for-my-future-hypothetical-daughter</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer296609396" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer851787443880190"><br/>My favorite thing about this book is, of course, <b>Wyverary A-Through-L</b>. What's a wyverary, you ask? Well, <b>when a wyvern and a library love each other very very much...</b>...blush... you know the spiel.<br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380372683i/726014.jpg' width='400' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/>--------------------------------------------------------------<br/>But do I sense some skepticism, my cynical friends? <b>Do you maybe insist on thinking there is an infinitely more prosaic explanation for the existence of Wyverary, an alphabetizing-loving fire-breathing half-library?</b> Let him rebuke your doubt</span>
  <span id="freeText851787443880190" style="display:none"><br>My favorite thing about this book is, of course, <b>Wyverary A-Through-L</b>. What's a wyverary, you ask? Well, <b>when a wyvern and a library love each other very very much...</b>...blush... you know the spiel.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380372683i/726014.jpg" width="400" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>--------------------------------------------------------------<br>But do I sense some skepticism, my cynical friends? <b>Do you maybe insist on thinking there is an infinitely more prosaic explanation for the existence of Wyverary, an alphabetizing-loving fire-breathing half-library?</b> Let him rebuke your doubts himself: <blockquote>
  <i> September, really. Which do you think is more likely? That some brute bull left my mother with egg and went off to sell lonemozers, or that she mated with a Library and had many loved and loving children? <b>I mean, let us be realistic!</b></i>
</blockquote> This is a cute and whimsical story of a pre-teen Nebraska girl September (born in May, actually) who eagerly leaves the world where her father is fighting in a war and her mother is building airplanes, and sets out for Fairyland. Where, as she soon learns, things are not all that she had thought they'd be. <b>There is violence, and slavery, and pain, and abandonment, and cruelty, and bureaucracy.</b> <blockquote>
  <i>I believe I am sick to death of hearing what is and is not allowed. What is the purpose of a Fairyland if everything lovely is outlawed, just like in the real world?</i>
</blockquote> Along the way, September meets the aforementioned Wyverary, a wish-granting Marid, the evil Marquess, spoonless witches, queenless soap golem, migrating velocipedes, and a jacket that is eager to please, among others. <b>Along the way, she loses her heart, her shadow, her friends, and a great deal of her innocence. And finds much more than she lost - or bargained for.</b> <blockquote>
  <i>Oh, September. Such lonely, lost things you find on your way. It would be easier, if you were the only one lost. But lost children always find each other, in the dark, in the cold. It is as though they are magnetized, and can only attract their like. [...] If you would only leave cages locked and turn away from unloved Wyverns, you could stay Heartless. But you are stubborn, and do not listen to your elders. </i>
</blockquote> This story is marketed for children, but I think it takes an adult to fully appreciate the scope of this story as well as many more-or-less subtle adult hints scattered throughout. <b>The book is permeated with the nostalgia for childhood and innocence, and you can truly appreciate this nostalgia only after you have left your childhood behind.</b><br><br>The writing and the plotting of this book reminded me of a hybrid between the creations of Lewis Carroll (<i>with less whimsy</i>), Terry Pratchett (<i>but less firmly grounded in the unreal reality</i>), and Neil Gaiman (<i>with less of the trademark matter-of-fact coolness</i>). At first I thought it was trying too hard to be cute and self-aware, a bit too flowery, with overly precocious allegories and endless whimsy. Example: <blockquote>
  <i>You’ll know it right away, it’s a big wooden spoon, streaked with marrow and wine and sugar and yogurt and yesterday and grief and passion and jealousy and tomorrow.</i>
</blockquote> But the writing grew on me as I continued with the story, and I came to love the fluidity of language and the beauty and lyricism of Valente's apt descriptions. The plot moves along smoothly and in determined fashion - much like September does through the Fairyland. <br><br>.....<img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380372683i/726015.jpg" width="300" height="220" class="gr-hostedUserImg">.....<br><br>As for our heroine September - she is pretty cool and awesome. She is kind and resourceful and brave and stubborn and spirited. But I must admit - I did not care for her as much as I did for Gaiman's Coraline or Pratchett's Tiffany Aching - but in all honesty, those characters are hard to compete with. I cared more for her quest than for her. <b>But the supporting characters truly shine. </b> <blockquote>
  <i>That’s the way I’m made. I have to keep going, always, and even when I get where I’m going I’ll have to keep on.</i>
</blockquote> <b>The strange and somewhat broken Fairyland has won me over.</b> I recommend this book to everyone who loves to exercise their imagination with a bot of whimsy. Plus, you will get to meet my favorite Wyverary! <b>4.5 stars, and it is placed on my "For-my-future-hypothetical-daughter" shelf.</b> <blockquote>
<i>Stories have a way of changing faces. They are unruly things, undisciplined, given to delinquency and the throwing of erasers. This is why we must close them up into thick, solid books, so they cannot get out and cause trouble.</i> </blockquote><br>........................<br>My review for the second September book, <i>The Girl Who Fell Beneath Fairyland and Led the Revels There</i>, is <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/298108143" rel="nofollow noopener">over here</a>, by the way.</span>
  <a data-text-id="851787443880190" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_177006466" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/177006466" />
    <a title="carol. " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3978225-carol"><img alt="carol. " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1307934801p2/3978225.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/177006466?book_show_action=true">Jun 15, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="carol. " class="user" itemprop="url" name="carol. " href="/user/show/3978225-carol">carol. </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">fans of wardrobes, YA fans</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3978225-carol?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3978225-carol?shelf=my-library-hardcover">my-library-hardcover</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3978225-carol?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3978225-carol?shelf=awards">awards</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3978225-carol?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3978225-carol?shelf=my-library">my-library</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer177006466" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8908567834030672226">The first two pages and I'm in love. <br/><br/>It's going on the "must buy" list, as well as the "must give" list.<br/><br/>The Girl sets all fairy tale conventions on their heads while managing to retain the spirit and charm of the best. In the tradition of the door-in-the-hedge fantasy, the trip through the closet into Fairyland is inventive and whimsical. Valente perhaps pokes fun at times, but always gently:<b> "you will either perish most painfully or be forced to sit through a very tedious tea service with sever</b></span>
  <span id="freeText8908567834030672226" style="display:none">The first two pages and I'm in love. <br /><br />It's going on the "must buy" list, as well as the "must give" list.<br /><br />The Girl sets all fairy tale conventions on their heads while managing to retain the spirit and charm of the best. In the tradition of the door-in-the-hedge fantasy, the trip through the closet into Fairyland is inventive and whimsical. Valente perhaps pokes fun at times, but always gently:<b> "you will either perish most painfully or be forced to sit through a very tedious tea service with several spinster hamadryads." </b> The heroine is a bit unconventional but not exactly drowning in misery: <b>"she washed the same pink-and-yellow teacups and matching gravy boats every day, slept on the same embroidered pillow"</b> and had a mother <b>"bending over a stubborn airplane engine in her work overalls, her arm muscles bulging." </b>Right there, you know it won't be traditional, but nor will it be grim modern, with boys locked under staircases, mothers with drug problems, or orphaned children scavenging food. Yet it still explores the core emotional issues of independence, identity, fear, and love, while acknowledging the place children come from is not all kindness and cookies. <b>"One ought not to judge her: All children are heartless. They have not grown a heart yet, which is why they can climb tall trees and say shocking things and leap so very high that grown-up hearts flutter in terror. Hearts weigh quite a lot. That is why it takes so long to grow one."</b><br /><br />Swooning continued as I read. Valente tells beautiful word-smithy tales. A Wyvern named "A-Through-L" (his father is the Library) deserves the award for Best Fantasy Sidekick of the Year. There's even a list of reasons why: <b>"Thirdly, being French in origin, they have highly refined tastes and are unlikely to seek out unsavory things to eat, such as knights' gallbladders or maidens' bones. They much prefer a vat or two of truffles, a flock of geese, and a lake of wine, and they will certainly share."</b> Of course, since they are French.<br /><br />After finishing, I was mentally working out my review as I swam, and discovered I had trouble analyzing why I enjoyed this book so much. I went home, picked up the book again, opened to a page and found myself saying, "oh, I loved this part," only to follow it with, "and this phrasing!" and exclamations of "and look how she characterizes ___!"<br /><br />That's the kind of book it is: something you remember loving and enjoying, even when you can't quite identify why, and then when you are immersed in it again, it all becomes crystal clear.<br /><br />Like a fantasy world.<br /><b><br /><br />"When you are born... your courage is new and clean. You are brave enough for anything: crawling off of staircases, saying your first words without fearing that someone will think you are foolish, putting strange things in your mouth. But as you get older, your courage attracts gunk and crusty things and dirt and fear and knowing how bad things can get and what pain feels like. By the time you're half-grown, your courage barely moves at all, it's so grunged up with living."<br /><br />Cross posted at <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://clsiewert.wordpress.com/2012/12/26/the-girl-who-circumnavigated-fairyland-in-the-ship-of-her-own-making/">http://clsiewert.wordpress.com/2012/1...</a></b></span>
  <a data-text-id="8908567834030672226" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_160624875" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/160624875" />
    <a title="Krystle" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2639204-krystle"><img alt="Krystle" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1403921272p2/2639204.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/160624875?book_show_action=true">Apr 12, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Krystle" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Krystle" href="/user/show/2639204-krystle">Krystle</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2639204-krystle?shelf=did-not-finish">did-not-finish</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer160624875" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer29777064638806224">This book just wasn't for me. The writing style is so different, so whimsical, so fancy, that I can tell the author had a lot of fun stretching her vocabulary to the utmost and rolling around and playing in it till it came out in wonderfully wrapped paragraphs and pages. But I just didn't like it. There are so much <i>things</i> I had to remember, keep track of, and all that stuff that I just got so lost and became disinterested.<br/><br/>Don't get me wrong, the world building is creative and all sorts of fabulo</span>
  <span id="freeText29777064638806224" style="display:none">This book just wasn't for me. The writing style is so different, so whimsical, so fancy, that I can tell the author had a lot of fun stretching her vocabulary to the utmost and rolling around and playing in it till it came out in wonderfully wrapped paragraphs and pages. But I just didn't like it. There are so much <i>things</i> I had to remember, keep track of, and all that stuff that I just got so lost and became disinterested.<br /><br />Don't get me wrong, the world building is creative and all sorts of fabulous. It's got humor, funky creatures, and all sorts of cool stuff we all love. But it's kinda hard to visualize. For me, anyway.<br /><br />There's even threads of deeper themes in the book. Such as even though things seem wonderful on the outside, they may not be when one looks closer at it. The maturation and growth of one leaving childhood and learning about the hardships of the world. The things a girl lacks and then wants may actually be what she has in bountiful measures even though she can't readily see it so clearly.<br /><br />All this stuff. But I just wasn't into the story. I think it's the case of right book, wrong reader. I'm quite sure this book will have its scores of readers and that one shouldn't be deterred by my review. They should, of course, pick the book up themself and see if it's for them or not.<br /><br />I tried, I really tried. I got more than 150 pages through this book and once I realized that I just didn't care or connect with the characters and had begun skimming I knew it was time to put the book down. Sad I couldn't like it more but I guess that's how the world of books go.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="29777064638806224" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_198165770" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/198165770" />
    <a title="Catie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1886642-catie"><img alt="Catie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1385169623p2/1886642.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/198165770?book_show_action=true">Aug 13, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Catie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Catie" href="/user/show/1886642-catie">Catie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Catie by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/283407-crowinator">Crowinator</a>
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1886642-catie?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1886642-catie?shelf=ya">ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1886642-catie?shelf=audio">audio</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1886642-catie?shelf=read-in-2011">read-in-2011</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer198165770" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11647944666935413446">I am generally one for simple, blunt truth. My brain doesn’t like to decipher complex and ornate metaphors and I hate reading through layer upon layer of language. I’m usually just <i>waiting</i> for the author to <i>get to the point.</i> But then, something like this comes along and just makes me question everything that I thought I knew about myself. The writing here is highly imaginative and odd and funny and a bit absurd. It’s descriptive and clever and maybe occasionally just a bit fussy. But, all this s</span>
  <span id="freeText11647944666935413446" style="display:none">I am generally one for simple, blunt truth. My brain doesn’t like to decipher complex and ornate metaphors and I hate reading through layer upon layer of language. I’m usually just <i>waiting</i> for the author to <i>get to the point.</i> But then, something like this comes along and just makes me question everything that I thought I knew about myself. The writing here is highly imaginative and odd and funny and a bit absurd. It’s descriptive and clever and maybe occasionally just a bit fussy. But, all this shine and glimmer and show has some real substance underneath it. (And honestly…I liked the shine and glimmer most of the time. There isn’t one page of this book that I couldn’t pull a gorgeous quote from.) Ms. Valente certainly <i>does</i> “get to the point” and the point is real, honest, emotion and a gorgeous coming of age story.<br /><br />September is a twelve year old girl who finds her life dull and tedious, and so, when the Green Wind flows in one day with a flying Leopard to take her off to Fairyland, she goes without a thought. She doesn’t even spare a goodbye for her parents, who are both rather missing in her life anyway. In Fairyland she initially gets swept up in novelty and adventure, as she meets glorious new friends and takes on a random quest. But she soon realizes that all is not well: the Marquesse reigns, imposing strict taxes, restrictions, and bureaucracy on every citizen. <br /><br />The similarities to Alice in Wonderland are evident, but this book also makes little nods to many other notable fantasy series. (And I seriously doubt Alice would ever fashion her own boat out of fairy drift-scepters and then sail it bald and in the nude.) The writing reminds me of Neil Gaiman, or I think that if China Mieville had a sweet, optimistic little sister she might write a book like this. However, even with all of these nods, this book feels inventive and original.<br /><br />I do love fantasy that’s character-driven and relatable, but sometimes I <i>really</i> crave fantasy like this: where everything is brand new. I want to think about what it might be like to be born half a person, or created out of soap. I want to imagine that I can have my courage cleaned and find a jacket that loves me and cares for me. I want to know what kind of adventures my shadow would get up to if we were ever separated.<br /><br />But even with all of these oddities and inventions, this book has a strong undercurrent of the real. September’s growth and loss of innocence is so painful and so wonderful. I felt so much sympathy for Lye, left all alone without instruction, or Saturday, who must always be forced to submit. And I laughed with A through L, the stalwart wyvern-library hybrid. But the most affecting of all turned out to be someone I least expected. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Wow. The Queen Mallow/Marquesse story really moved me. I felt so betrayed and bitter on her behalf. That whole part is just brilliant. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br /><br /><u>Perfect Musical Pairing</u><br /><br />Joanna Newsom – <a href="http://www.youtube.com/watch?v=Jv4A6_EPo9o" rel="nofollow noopener">Bridges and Balloons</a><br /><br />“<i> We sailed away on a winter's day<br />With fate as malleable as clay”</i><br /><br />That about says it. This song is so quirky and oddly beautiful. I think that it's about risking a horrible fate to go out and live and see glorious sights. And I think that “funny little thing” might be the perfect description for this book.<br /><br />Also seen on <a href="http://www.thereadventurer.com/2/post/2012/04/mg-review-the-girl-who-circumnavigated-fairyland-in-a-ship-of-her-own-making-by-catherynne-m-valente.html" rel="nofollow noopener">The Readventurer</a>.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11647944666935413446" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1032761406" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1032761406" />
    <a title="Tadiana ✩Night Owl☽" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8734459-tadiana-night-owl"><img alt="Tadiana ✩Night Owl☽" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1603085284p2/8734459.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1032761406?book_show_action=true">Aug 21, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tadiana ✩Night Owl☽" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tadiana ✩Night Owl☽" href="/user/show/8734459-tadiana-night-owl">Tadiana ✩Night Owl☽</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8734459-tadiana-night-owl?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8734459-tadiana-night-owl?shelf=fairy-tale">fairy-tale</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8734459-tadiana-night-owl?shelf=library-has">library-has</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8734459-tadiana-night-owl?shelf=portal-fantasy">portal-fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1032761406" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13657672096112539510">This is a portal fantasy in the <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/236093.The_Wonderful_Wizard_of_Oz__Oz___1_' title='The Wonderful Wizard of Oz (Oz, #1) by L. Frank Baum' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Wonderful Wizard of Oz</a>/<a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/100915.The_Lion__the_Witch__and_the_Wardrobe__Chronicles_of_Narnia___1_' title='The Lion, the Witch, and the Wardrobe (Chronicles of Narnia, #1) by C.S. Lewis' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Lion, the Witch, and the Wardrobe</a> tradition, where a young girl goes to a magical land and tries to Right What's Wrong. <br/><br/>Twelve year old September, bored with her life and washing pink-and-yellow teacups and dealing with mostly-absent parents, gets talked into a trip to Fairyland by the Green Wind, who settles her into the saddle of his flying leopard and whisks her away to new adventures. Because--like most children--September is mor</span>
  <span id="freeText13657672096112539510" style="display:none">This is a portal fantasy in the <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/236093.The_Wonderful_Wizard_of_Oz__Oz___1_" title="The Wonderful Wizard of Oz (Oz, #1) by L. Frank Baum" rel="nofollow noopener">The Wonderful Wizard of Oz</a>/<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/100915.The_Lion__the_Witch__and_the_Wardrobe__Chronicles_of_Narnia___1_" title="The Lion, the Witch, and the Wardrobe (Chronicles of Narnia, #1) by C.S. Lewis" rel="nofollow noopener">The Lion, the Witch, and the Wardrobe</a> tradition, where a young girl goes to a magical land and tries to Right What's Wrong. <br><br>Twelve year old September, bored with her life and washing pink-and-yellow teacups and dealing with mostly-absent parents, gets talked into a trip to Fairyland by the Green Wind, who settles her into the saddle of his flying leopard and whisks her away to new adventures. Because--like most children--September is more or less Heartless, she doesn't tell her mother good-bye or leave her a note. She finds some delightful (and magical) friends and is reluctantly pulled into a quest by the cruel ruler of Fairyland, the Marquess. And September begins to grow a heart, which can be a painful process, especially if you are fated to lose it.<br><br>It's extremely fantastical and whimsical, and it was a little too much for me when I sat down and tried to read it straight through, but when I started reading it in smaller doses, with breaks in between, the delightfulness resurfaced. This would be a fun read-aloud book with children who are old enough to handle some painful scenes where characters get badly hurt. It's ultimately a very uplifting story with a good underlying message.<blockquote>"You are not the chosen one, September. Fairyland did not choose you--you chose yourself. You could have had a lovely holiday in Fairyland and never met the Marquess, never worried yourself with local politics, had a romp with a few brownies and gone home with enough memories for a lifetime's worth of novels. But you didn't. You chose. You chose it all."</blockquote>Reading <i>The Girl Who Circumnavigated Fairyland</i> is kind of like this:<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1417803045i/12550579._SX540_.jpg" width="320" height="240" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>and this:<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1417803045i/12550580._SX540_.jpg" width="320" height="180" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>with a little of this:<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1417803045i/12550581._SX540_.jpg" width="300" height="242" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1417803045i/12550582._SX540_.jpg" width="327" height="246" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>P.S. I highly recommend the prequel short story, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/11869878.The_Girl_Who_Ruled_Fairyland___For_a_Little_While__Fairyland___0_5_" title="The Girl Who Ruled Fairyland - For a Little While (Fairyland, #0.5) by Catherynne M. Valente" rel="nofollow noopener">The Girl Who Ruled Fairyland - For a Little While</a>. It's free online at Tor.com, and it's a great way to test the waters and see if this series is likely to appeal to you.<br><br>Art credits:<br><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://honour-mcmillan.blogspot.com/2010/06/sl7b-whimsy-wonder-and-wierd-part-1.html">http://honour-mcmillan.blogspot.com/2...</a><br><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://limsh.deviantart.com/art/Lulu-practicing-Whimsy-353397544">http://limsh.deviantart.com/art/Lulu-...</a><br><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.imagespalace.com/2013/06/impressive-whimsical-fantasy.html">http://www.imagespalace.com/2013/06/i...</a><br><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.mimitabby.com/blog/whimsy-cats">http://www.mimitabby.com/blog/whimsy-...</a></span>

<div id="review_248607043" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/248607043" />
    <a title="mark monday" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/131922-mark-monday"><img alt="mark monday" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1572672245p2/131922.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/248607043?book_show_action=true">Dec 18, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="mark monday" class="user" itemprop="url" name="mark monday" href="/user/show/131922-mark-monday">mark monday</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/131922-mark-monday?shelf=fantasy-modern">fantasy-modern</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/131922-mark-monday?shelf=inbetweenworld">inbetweenworld</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/131922-mark-monday?shelf=legendarium">legendarium</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer248607043" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9633376011786175471">growing up, i loved the Oz books (the Baum ones, at least). i read all of them multiple times - i think there are 14 or so - and have enjoyed rereading them here and there as an adult. i love how the fancifulness and frequent absurdity of Baum's creations are anchored down by prosaic reality. i love their no-nonsense child heroines (and occasional heroes) - precocious but never precious, cute but never cutesy-poo. i love the transparency of Baum's prose, the layering of meaning and metaphor, the</span>
  <span id="freeText9633376011786175471" style="display:none">growing up, i loved the Oz books (the Baum ones, at least). i read all of them multiple times - i think there are 14 or so - and have enjoyed rereading them here and there as an adult. i love how the fancifulness and frequent absurdity of Baum's creations are anchored down by prosaic reality. i love their no-nonsense child heroines (and occasional heroes) - precocious but never precious, cute but never cutesy-poo. i love the transparency of Baum's prose, the layering of meaning and metaphor, the use of genuine tragedy, the light touch, the wisdom of it all. so it is a happy thing and one of the highest compliments that i can imagine giving when i say that reading Girl Who Circumnavigated brought me right back to that enchanting feeling of reading a classic Oz book.<br /><br />Valente is a marvel with language. i knew she could write like a mad poet after reading the amazing <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/202769.In_the_Night_Garden?utm_medium=api&amp;utm_source=blog_book" rel="nofollow noopener">In the Night Garden</a>; less expected was her ability to smooth down and simplify her lush style so that it is perfectly tailored for a children's novel. it loses no lustre in the transition. reading Valente's prose reminds me of looking through my window at a light rain falling on an otherwise bright day, the sun and water making a painting of the world, images seen through the droplets of rain rolling down glass. lovely!<br /><br />the character of The Girl Who Circumnavigates is instantly familiar from any number of Oz books - her sensible and at times irritable nature, the depth of her feelings, her forthright way of navigating the places through which she wanders. she is a classic type, but never a tiresome one. her attachment to her new friends is adorable, but never corny or mawkish. i love the brave moments when she considers returning home but almost instantaneously rejects that cowardly path. and when she finally builds that Ship of Her Own Making... my gosh, that was wonderful! much internal cheering ensued.<br /><br />Valente makes the adventure a pleasure from beginning to end. her use of irony is constant - and sweetly good-humored, never heavy-handed, suitable for kids but thoroughly <i>adult</i> as well. equally sophisticated is her use of symbol and metaphor, her smooth incorporation of various mythologies and mythological creatures, and especially her entirely original conception of the novel's arch-villain - so appalling, so tragic, so understandable. poor child!<br /><br />and any children's fantasy that features the parallel saga of a brave &amp; loyal Key, a strikingly sinister Shadow of a Little Girl about to run off on its own strange journey, a helpful &amp; industrious Smoking Jacket, two Witches married to an elegant little male Witch/ Wair-Wolf, and most of all a genuinely touching &amp; loveable Wyvern... well, i am that novel's true friend.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9633376011786175471" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="friendReviews elementListBrown" >
    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_165403453" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/165403453" />
    <a title="Betsy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/221050-betsy"><img alt="Betsy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442631153p2/221050.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/165403453?book_show_action=true">May 03, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Betsy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Betsy" href="/user/show/221050-betsy">Betsy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer165403453" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11126535514328033328">Well devil if I know what to do with it.<br/><br/>Never complain that you are bored, ladies and gentlemen. Say such a thing and you might find that the universe has a couple tricks up its sleeve. Let's say, for example, that a certain children's librarian was getting bored with the state of fantasy today. Maybe she read too many Narnia rip-offs where a group of siblings is plunged into an alternate world to defeat a big bad blah blah blah. Maybe she read too many quest novels where plucky young girls have</span>
  <span id="freeText11126535514328033328" style="display:none">Well devil if I know what to do with it.<br /><br />Never complain that you are bored, ladies and gentlemen. Say such a thing and you might find that the universe has a couple tricks up its sleeve. Let's say, for example, that a certain children's librarian was getting bored with the state of fantasy today. Maybe she read too many Narnia rip-offs where a group of siblings is plunged into an alternate world to defeat a big bad blah blah blah. Maybe she read too many quest novels where plucky young girls have to save their brothers/friends/housepets. So what does the universe do? Does it say, "Maybe you should try something other than fantasy for a change"? It does not. Instead it hands the children's librarian a book with a title like <i>The Girl Who Circumnavigated Fairyland in a Ship of Her Own Making</i> and (if she hasn't hyperventilated after reading the title) says to her, "Here you go, smart guy. Try this on for size." That's what being cocky will get you. It'll have you reading a book that walks up to the usual middle grade chapter book fantasy tropes and slaps 'em right smack dab in the face. I have never, in all my livelong days, read a book quite like Catherynne Valente's. My job now is to figure out whether that is a good thing, or very very bad.<br /><br />When September is asked by The Green Wind whether or not she'd be inclined to take a trip to Fairyland with him, she's so excited to get going that she manages to lose a shoe in the process. Like many a good reader September is inclined to think that she knows the rules of alternate worlds. Yet it doesn't take much time before she realizes that not all things are well in the realm of magic. A strange Marquess has taken over, having defeated the previous good ruler, and before she knows it September is sent to try to retrieve a spoon from the all powerful villain. Along the way she befriends a Wyvern who is certain that his father was a library, and a strange blue Marid boy named Saturday who can grant you a wish, but only if you defeat him in a fight. With their help, Saturday realizes what it means to lose your heart within the process of becoming less heartless.<br /><br />Divisive. Each year you'll encounter one big children's book that can be labeled as such. Certain books and certain writers can have violent affects on their readers, unsuspected until the official reviews start pouring in. Then suddenly folks with opinions start pouring out of the woodwork. The books are as varied as <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6596547-mockingbird" rel="nofollow noopener">Mockingbird</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/2768169.The_Underneath" title="The Underneath by Kathi Appelt" rel="nofollow noopener">The Underneath</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/37186.The_Miraculous_Journey_of_Edward_Tulane" title="The Miraculous Journey of Edward Tulane by Kate DiCamillo" rel="nofollow noopener">The Miraculous Journey of Edward Tulane</a> or <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/39999.The_Boy_in_the_Striped_Pajamas" title="The Boy in the Striped Pajamas by John Boyne" rel="nofollow noopener">The Boy in the Striped Pajamas</a>. One thing's for certain, though. Everyone has an opinion. This year I've only identified two potentially divisive books and one of them is the title you see before you today. I know I've been a little cagey about what I thought of it until now so here's the 411: I like it. A lot. Far more than I thought that I would, particularly after that first chapter. As far as I can determine, enjoying this book means getting through Chapter One. If you read the first chapter and find yourself throwing the book against the wall without restraint, this may not be the story for you. If, however, you feel a vague queasiness that resolves itself into reluctant curiosity, you may wish to continue. And if you do, you will find a title that really outdoes itself in being . . . well . . . it's own very one-of-a-kind self.<br /><br />But why is it divisive? It all comes down to Valente's language. Look, here's the first sentence as an example: "Once upon a time, a girl named September grew very tired indeed of her parents' house, where she washed the same pink-and-yellow teacups and matching gravy boats every day, slept on the same embroidered pillow, and played with the same small and amiable dog." About ten words into that sentence you had to make a decision on whether or not to continue reading. Here's some advice on going through this book. Step One: Get a grasp on its internal logic.<br /><br />The <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6983471-the-complete-alice" rel="nofollow noopener">Alice's Adventures in Wonderland</a> comparison is inevitable. Generally speaking, a person is able to identify a poor debut children's book when the author attempts to make an Alice-in-Wonderland-but-with-a-twist book. The problem with this plan is that just as no band sounds quite like The Beatles, no children's novel ever sounds quite like <i>Alice</i>. They try, oh Lord they try, but no go. More often than not such books are instead tedious and very poorly done. Most of them think that the lure of <i>Alice</i> is strange talking creatures in a world with no rules. This is somewhat true, but it's only a piece of the puzzle. And in all my days as a children's librarian, reading fantasy after fantasy, I have NEVER encountered a book that came as close to <i>Alice</i> as this. Not because Valente also throws a girl into a fairyland with kooky characters, but because it is so infinitely clear that she loves to play with language. Logic isn't as twisted up as it is in Carroll's universe, but that's all right. Valente is comfortable weaving her own unique vision, and like Carroll she's not afraid to throw in a little joke for adults once in a while. Would a kid get anything out of reading that the Green Wind possesses a "golden ring of diplomatic immunity"? Probably not and they probably won't care when Saturday enters a delicious looking town that, "was as though the witch who built the gingerbread house in the story had a great number of friends and decided to start up a collective." But it won't hurt the reading experience either.<br /><br />Of course September is far more active than Alice when seeking out her adventure. In fact, if I were to compare her to any famous children's literary character, she probably bears more in common with Milo from <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/378.The_Phantom_Tollbooth" title="The Phantom Tollbooth by Norton Juster" rel="nofollow noopener">The Phantom Tollbooth</a> than anyone else. That was my first thought. Then after a while I decided that September begins as Alice (after all, she lies right at the start about wanting to go home), morphs into Dorothy (girl + faithful companions to defeat the big bad villain), and comes to us by way of Milo (boredom as a storytelling impetus). That's a pretty pedigree. On top of that, this is a thoroughly American fantasy. One where you won't encounter random characters with cockney accents (a current pet peeve of mine). September hails from Omaha, Nebraska and the story seems to take place during WWII. Her father is stationed in Europe while her mother works in the factories at home. Many fantasies for kids eschew placing their stories in such distinctive time periods, but if it worked for Narnia it should work here too.<br /><br />And Valente gets personalities down rather well too. I heard one complaint that the Marid named Saturday is hardly a fleshed out character. I might contest this, though, since I found him capable of many small touches that rang clear and true to me. For example, at one point he makes a point that is followed up with the notation, "He was still too shy to suggest anything without wrapping it up tight to keep it safe." Likewise the villain of this book is delicious. It takes a while to get a good grasp on the Marquess, but once you get her full backstory then there's a lot to admire here. A mere two-dimensional villain she is not, and for that I was grateful.<br /><br />Ana Juan, brilliant Ana Juan, could not have been a better person to draw the interstitial illustrations that appear at the beginnings of each and every chapter. This Spanish illustrator specializes in dreamlike worlds on her own time ("The Night Eater" is a perfect example) so it is interesting to see what she does with a book like Valente's. To my surprise, she hones in her talents a bit. The pictures here are most definitely her own, but there's a tendency here to make them a little younger and clearer than I'm used to seeing. There's a darkness to Valente's story that does not replicate itself in the pictures, which is probably a good thing. After all, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/146.Quentin_Blake" title="Quentin Blake" rel="nofollow noopener">Quentin Blake</a>'s illustrations have always served to make <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/4273.Roald_Dahl" title="Roald Dahl" rel="nofollow noopener">Roald Dahl</a> less frightening at times. Maybe Juan's are doing the same thing here.<br /><br />In the end, it's all about the language and the inevitable question of whether or not kids will dig the book. It's a worthy question. When a character is sent to a fairyland, even one in dire straits, it is up to the author to make it clear that this is a place you would want to visit. Some fantasies go a shade too dark and because of this inclination do not become beloved by children. Valente, however, mixes some wonderful elements with some horrific ones well enough that I think this book could be fondly remembered by a child years and years later. And when they return to it as adults, how surprised they will be by the wordplay. I won't lie. Some folks do NOT like this book, and I can understand why that is. For me, though, this is just one of the smarter juxtapositions of the fantastical with the tongue-twisted. Here you have an author who clearly enjoys writing. And if that enjoyment seeps through the page and into the reader's perceptions, then here is a book that they'll clearly enjoy <i>reading</i>. A true original and like nothing you've really ever seen before.<br /><br />For ages 9-12. </span>
  <a data-text-id="11126535514328033328" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

<span id="freeTextContainer8176905882002190065">I didn't properly finish the book because I couldn't bring myself to care about what happened to the main character. Or, rather, I feel like I already know: September is going to keep encountering a string of creatures, except [creature] is <em>totally different</em> from any other rendition of [creature] in literature, and will spend some time pedantically explaining itself and its neuroses, there'll be a lot of forced wackiness, and she'll pick up clues and bits of string and solve whatever at the end </span>
  <span id="freeText8176905882002190065" style="display:none">I didn't properly finish the book because I couldn't bring myself to care about what happened to the main character. Or, rather, I feel like I already know: September is going to keep encountering a string of creatures, except [creature] is <em>totally different</em> from any other rendition of [creature] in literature, and will spend some time pedantically explaining itself and its neuroses, there'll be a lot of forced wackiness, and she'll pick up clues and bits of string and solve whatever at the end and click her heels and go home and I'm so bored. It was overwhelmingly <em>writerly</em>, and while I appreciate a well-turned phrase as well as the next person, Valente is jumping in front of me, waving her hands in my face, 'Look at <em>me</em>! I'm so <em>clever</em>! I have a <em>thesaurus</em> and an appreciation of Lewis Carroll!' so that I can't even see the story.</span>

<div id="review_1398370516" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1398370516" />
    <a title="Bradley" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4213258-bradley"><img alt="Bradley" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1508811508p2/4213258.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1398370516?book_show_action=true">Sep 22, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Bradley" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Bradley" href="/user/show/4213258-bradley">Bradley</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4213258-bradley?shelf=worldbuilding-sf">worldbuilding-sf</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4213258-bradley?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4213258-bradley?shelf=ya">ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4213258-bradley?shelf=2016-shelf">2016-shelf</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1398370516" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13071667605134366786">This is easily one of the most delightful and magical YA titles I've ever read.<br/><br/>I know people do like to compare it to Alice in Wonderland, but in a lot of ways, it's better. There's more than a basketful of clever, more than a truckload of beautiful language, and a whole ocean of delight.<br/><br/>The darkness doesn't overwhelm and there's no overt or subtle religious messages. A lot happens, but it's friendship that carries the final day. <br/><br/>I'm going to be reading this to my daughter when she is a little o</span>
  <span id="freeText13071667605134366786" style="display:none">This is easily one of the most delightful and magical YA titles I've ever read.<br /><br />I know people do like to compare it to Alice in Wonderland, but in a lot of ways, it's better. There's more than a basketful of clever, more than a truckload of beautiful language, and a whole ocean of delight.<br /><br />The darkness doesn't overwhelm and there's no overt or subtle religious messages. A lot happens, but it's friendship that carries the final day. <br /><br />I'm going to be reading this to my daughter when she is a little older. I honestly think it surpasses Pullman and Gaiman and Carroll. It's so light and it tickles all my funny-bones.<br /><br />And best of all, it leaves no aftertaste except for a pleasant glow. No saccarine. No pedantic moralizing. Just plain magic, trickery, adventure, and a twist of the tongue that makes me grin from ear to ear.<br /><br />Valente is quickly becoming one of my most beloved authors. I knew I had to read everything after <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/18490533.Radiance" title="Radiance by Catherynne M. Valente" rel="nofollow noopener">Radiance</a>, and this just cements it. :)</span>
  <a data-text-id="13071667605134366786" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>
