<div id="review_1491142977" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1491142977" />
    <a title="Trish" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3461034-trish"><img alt="Trish" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1588663568p2/3461034.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1491142977?book_show_action=true">Jan 02, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Trish" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Trish" href="/user/show/3461034-trish">Trish</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1491142977" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12834558546879204783"><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1447864068i/17059580.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/>I found this picture some time ago but had no idea how fitting it would be for this review (the text as well as the little girl pictured)! :D<br/><br/>In fact, I only decided to buy and read this book because of Brad's raving review and the fact that I was able to get it for my Kindle for just 99 Cents! Sometimes it really does seem as if some books were meant to be with me and are willing to do anything to make that happen!<br/><br/>Anyway, this is the story of a girl called September who lives in Omaha and wishes</span>
  <span id="freeText12834558546879204783" style="display:none"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1447864068i/17059580.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>I found this picture some time ago but had no idea how fitting it would be for this review (the text as well as the little girl pictured)! :D<br><br>In fact, I only decided to buy and read this book because of Brad's raving review and the fact that I was able to get it for my Kindle for just 99 Cents! Sometimes it really does seem as if some books were meant to be with me and are willing to do anything to make that happen!<br><br>Anyway, this is the story of a girl called September who lives in Omaha and wishes herself away. I think we can all relate to that even if we do not live in Omaha. <br>Her wish is granted and thus begins her adventure in Fairyland.<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380385870r/744971._SX540_SY540_.jpg" width="400" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>The story itself is thrilling and adventuresome but, naturally, reminds the reader of other child-gets-to-fantasy-world-and-has-adventures stories. In fact, what was quite the gem while reading this book, was that the author references books like the Narnia series, Alice's Wonderland and Dorothy's Land of Oz and one could argue that she showed these to be all the same place, really.<br><br>However, this is NOT a typical book. Far from it. It's also not a copy/mix of the above mentioned books. <br>The author truly is a mage - and I don't say this often. Books about magical lands should also have magical words describing said magical world. And this author, so far as I can tell, is definitely one of the best when it comes to a magical language. Maybe she even is THE best of them. There are so many quotable lines that I'm certain I have marked at least 1/4 of the book if not more.<br>She uses puns, twists fairytale morals/tropes and she weaves all of it into a compelling description that makes your mouth water when you read about all sorts of autumnal food, <br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1452950974i/17764428.jpg" width="400" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>that lets you relax when you read about baths the main character takes and that lets you feel the wind in your own hair when September flies.<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380349939i/703875.jpg" width="400" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>Moreover, how the author spun her tale around the Marquess (not just a villain but actually a complicated character as is only right) and Fairyland's history shows that she cannot only tell a BEAUTIFUL tale but also a COMPLEX and CLEVER one. And a quirky, silly, funny, dark one too. <br>Seriously, this tale has so many layers, it is hard to do it justice when describing it. <br><br>I will admit that I had my doubts in the beginning when the author said that <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[children are heartless <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> since I thought this to be very odd and very false. But I think I just had the wrong sort of expectations from that line and very soon afterwards the words had bound me and swept me away and when we came to <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[The House Without Warning <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> I was utterly spellbound. That scene with <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Lye and the many different fairy baths <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> was the most beautiful and magical thing I've ever read and I loved it! It's my favourite part in the book, closely followed by <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[the everlasting autumn with the great wedding feast (I was soooo hungry when reading about all that wonderful food), woods, Halloween and death/September's transformation.<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1452950974i/17764429.png" width="400" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> since that is my favourite time of year!<br><br>Moreover, this book is made even more precious (if such a thing is possible) with the odd illustrations at the beginning of every chapter. Odd because of the proportions of the characters but that somehow fits the odd place that is Fairyland I think. However, just like the story isn't just clever or colourful, the illustrations are not just odd but rich with details.<br>And the mini-summary of what happens in the respective chapter underneath the illustration to said chapter is quite a nice touch as well because it makes the whole thing even more thrilling and makes one even more curious.<br>And how could I have not loved a story with so many different big cats?!<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1452950974i/17764430._SX540_.jpg" width="400" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>
  <a data-text-id="12834558546879204783" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer155460206" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15496794206789983944">It's hard to express in words just how lovely this book is, well, in <i>my</i> words that is; Valente's words are beyond magical.<blockquote>She certainly did not see Death stand on her tip-toes and blow a kiss after her, a kiss that rushed through all the frosted leaves of the autumnal forest but could not quite catch a child running as fast as she could. As all mothers know, children travel faster than kisses. The speed of kisses is, in fact, what Doctor Fallow would call a cosmic constant. The speed of children</blockquote></span>
  <span id="freeText15496794206789983944" style="display:none">It's hard to express in words just how lovely this book is, well, in <i>my</i> words that is; Valente's words are beyond magical.<blockquote>She certainly did not see Death stand on her tip-toes and blow a kiss after her, a kiss that rushed through all the frosted leaves of the autumnal forest but could not quite catch a child running as fast as she could. As all mothers know, children travel faster than kisses. The speed of kisses is, in fact, what Doctor Fallow would call a cosmic constant. The speed of children has no limits.</blockquote><b>If you love fantasy or fairy tales, you will fall head-over-heels in love with this book.</b><br /><br />Reading the last pages gave me the immense pleasure of shivers and goosebumps. This is a truly special book and I hope the majority of my friends read it.<br /><br />The <a href="http://www.youtube.com/watch?v=HU4q8dpKhDY&amp;feature=player_embedded" rel="nofollow noopener">book trailer</a> is also a wonderful thing to check out before <i>and</i> after you finish reading, and it successfully portrays the dark beauty of this book more so than I ever could with just a review.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15496794206789983944" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

    <a title="Maxwell" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1381728-maxwell"><img alt="Maxwell" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1539318702p2/1381728.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1813483817?book_show_action=true">Nov 19, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Maxwell" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Maxwell" href="/user/show/1381728-maxwell">Maxwell</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/10859388-the-girl-who-circumnavigated-fairyland-in-a-ship-of-her-own-making">review of another edition</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1813483817" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3573330840217891487">This is surely a whimsical and wonderful take on a classic fairytale. Valente also writes beautifully and challenges the reader (particularly young readers, the intended audience) with big words and big themes. I appreciated the grittiness of this story too. September, our heroine, faces some difficulties that you don't often find in children's literature. However, the middle of the story really lagged for me. There were a few chapters that didn't seem to contribute much to the plot other than t</span>
  <span id="freeText3573330840217891487" style="display:none">This is surely a whimsical and wonderful take on a classic fairytale. Valente also writes beautifully and challenges the reader (particularly young readers, the intended audience) with big words and big themes. I appreciated the grittiness of this story too. September, our heroine, faces some difficulties that you don't often find in children's literature. However, the middle of the story really lagged for me. There were a few chapters that didn't seem to contribute much to the plot other than to drag it out, and that was a shame because every other element of the story seemed so meticulously chosen and expertly placed. Overall I'm glad I finally saw what everyone was raving about; it's definitely an important story that I'm glad exists for young readers. I'm not sure if I will continue with the series any time soon, but maybe someday I'll return to fairyland.</span>

<div id="review_467069306" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/467069306" />
    <a title="Heidi The Reader" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7986781-heidi-the-reader"><img alt="Heidi The Reader" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1593309467p2/7986781.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/467069306?book_show_action=true">Oct 14, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Heidi The Reader" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Heidi The Reader" href="/user/show/7986781-heidi-the-reader">Heidi The Reader</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7986781-heidi-the-reader?shelf=fantasy-and-sci-fi">fantasy-and-sci-fi</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7986781-heidi-the-reader?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7986781-heidi-the-reader?shelf=the-numinous-book-club">the-numinous-book-club</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7986781-heidi-the-reader?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer467069306" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16372814891096996053"><i>The Girl Who Circumnavigated Fairyland in a Ship of Her Own Making</i> is a modern take on more traditional fairy tales wherein a child finds a way to another world and comes back changed.<br/><br/>I first read the title of this book in Catherynne Valente's much more adult novel <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/3973532.Palimpsest' title='Palimpsest by Catherynne M. Valente' rel='nofollow noopener'>Palimpsest</a>. I think it was mentioned as sitting on someone's book shelf. I remember thinking how I wish I could read that book too. Imagine my surprise to discover it was actually a book in the real world. Of course, I had to pick it </span>
  <span id="freeText16372814891096996053" style="display:none"><i>The Girl Who Circumnavigated Fairyland in a Ship of Her Own Making</i> is a modern take on more traditional fairy tales wherein a child finds a way to another world and comes back changed.<br /><br />I first read the title of this book in Catherynne Valente's much more adult novel <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/3973532.Palimpsest" title="Palimpsest by Catherynne M. Valente" rel="nofollow noopener">Palimpsest</a>. I think it was mentioned as sitting on someone's book shelf. I remember thinking how I wish I could read that book too. Imagine my surprise to discover it was actually a book in the real world. Of course, I had to pick it up.<br /><br /><i>"You seem an ill-tempered and irascible enough child," said the Green Wind. "How would you like to come away with me and ride upon the Leopard of Little Breezes and be delivered to the great sea, which borders Fairyland?"</i> pg 2<br /><br />How could any heroine refuse an invitation like that? And the main character of this tale, a girl with the curious name of September, has read enough books to know a once-in-a-lifetime chance when she sees it. Though she doubts, at first, that she is the appropriate girl for the adventure.<br /><br /><i>"In stories, when someone appears in a poof of green clouds and asks a girl to go away on an adventure, it's because she's special, because she's smart and strong and can solve riddles and fight with swords and give really good speeches, and... I don't know that I'm any of those things."</i> pg 14<br /><br />Part of Valente's fairytale, like most good fairytales, is how September realizes how special she actually is — one of the conclusions heroes tend to arrive at during their various journeys.<br /><br />September's journey is a danger-filled jaunt through a land under the thumb of a smartly-hatted villain named the Marquess. September meets curious characters along the way including a trio of witches, a wyvern who claims his father is a library, and a boy from under the ocean with dark eyes and a secret.<br /><br />The story contains plenty of winks and nods to anyone who loves reading: <i>"Stories have a way of changing faces. They are unruly things, undisciplined, given to delinquency and the throwing of erasers. This is why we must close them up into thick, solid books, so they cannot get out and cause trouble."</i> pg 36<br /><br />And: <i>"She sounds like someone who spends a lot of time in libraries, which are the best sorts of people."</i> pg 55<br /><br />They are the best sorts, aren't they.<br /><br />Recommended for young adults, the young-at-heart, or anyone who enjoys quirky portal fantasy reads. I thought this book was charming.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16372814891096996053" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="friendReviews elementListBrown" >
    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_317667658" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/317667658" />
    <a title="Jim" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4089478-jim"><img alt="Jim" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1315759484p2/4089478.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/317667658?book_show_action=true">Apr 23, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jim" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jim" href="/user/show/4089478-jim">Jim</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Those who can think young</span></div>

          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Jim by: </span>
      Catie and Nataliya
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4089478-jim?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4089478-jim?shelf=kids-miscellaneous">kids-miscellaneous</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4089478-jim?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer317667658" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10600558935582908943"><i>“If you want your children to be intelligent, read them fairy tales. If you want them to be more intelligent, read them more fairy tales.When I examine myself and my methods of thought, I come to the conclusion that the gift of fantasy has meant more to me than any talent for abstract, positive thinking.”</i><br/>― Albert Einstein<br/><br/>In the normal scheme of things, I would have read this “children’s book”* first, as my introduction to the amazing writing of Catherynne Valente. But because this physical book </span>
  <span id="freeText10600558935582908943" style="display:none"><i>“If you want your children to be intelligent, read them fairy tales. If you want them to be more intelligent, read them more fairy tales.When I examine myself and my methods of thought, I come to the conclusion that the gift of fantasy has meant more to me than any talent for abstract, positive thinking.”</i><br>― Albert Einstein<br><br>In the normal scheme of things, I would have read this “children’s book”* first, as my introduction to the amazing writing of Catherynne Valente. But because this physical book took longer than expected to arrive - and because I was already bitten by the Valente bug through my good friends Catie and Nataliya - I began by taking on the highly complex and challenging (though shorter) AI fantasy - <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/12887497.Silently_and_Very_Fast" title="Silently and Very Fast by Catherynne M. Valente" rel="nofollow noopener">Silently and Very Fast</a>. <br><br>Having read the complex novella, I expected this ‘simple’ middle-grade fantasy to be a leisurely cruise by comparison. Easy Peasy.<br><br>Silly me. Catherynne Valente, in my two-book experience, does not do Easy. Her writing is rich, layered, packed with ideas and playful, all at the same time and often in the same sentence. If you are looking for an easy read, look elsewhere.<br><br>But that’s okay by me, because I LOVE that kind of writing as long as it works on its own terms. By that, I mean I can handle the occasional sentence that needs to be read 2 or 3 times. I can unpack it, see the parts and understand the whole, admire what I see, and be ready for more. <br><br>Even so, I place a heavy burden on the author who writes that way. There must be beauty in the language and meaning in the lines. I need to care about the protagonist, and do a minimum of cringing over the latest stupid thing she has done. In the best case, she doesn’t do stupid things - or learns very quickly when she does. A no-argghhh narrative, that’s what I want.<br><br>Valente succeeds brilliantly on those terms, in my view. I would be hard-pressed to think of another author who displays the sheer power of beauty AND substance that she does. It is simply dazzling to watch her prose come to life, dance off the page and into sparkling structures that whirl off in all directions. I can’t get enough of it, and I intend to read a lot more (hopefully all) of her work.<br><br>In this Andre Norton Award winning tale, a 12 year old girl named September has a difficult and dreary life, full of mundane routine and with parents who are off to war (father) or working in war industry (mother). <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380375866i/730551.jpg" width="400" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>With thanks to THT and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/155460206" rel="nofollow noopener">her moving review</a>, I have borrowed a few stills from the <a href="http://www.youtube.com/watch?v=HU4q8dpKhDY&amp;feature=player_embedded" rel="nofollow noopener"> book trailer</a> for this amazing work. I thank THT for the link, and I want to repeat her recommendation to watch the video both before and after reading, if and when.<br><br>September gets an invitation to ride off to Fairyland, and accepts with minimal hesitation - whether in her thoughts and dreams, or in a realistic fantasy, Valente is artfully unclear.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380375866i/730552._SX540_.jpg" width="500" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><i>”Ever so briefly, Latitude and Longitude kissed, and when they parted, there was a space between their mouths just large enough for a Leopard carrying a Harsh Air and a little girl.”</i><br><br>From there, a series of adventures unfolds, with a master fantasist at the controls. We tour a series of richly imagined creations, and meet a fascinating set of characters that any author would envy and most readers will love. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380375866i/730553.jpg" width="500" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Fairyland is full of wonders, but governed by rigid bureaucratic principles. September is only a young girl, with no experience of any of these things, but she must make do and accomplish what seems impossible, to her and to us. <br> <br><i>”The going was not easy. Gold is very slippery to walk on and insists on sliding all over the place. She found that her bare foot was actually a bit more suited to the task than the shod one, as she could grasp at the gleaming ground with her toes.”</i><br><br>She shows remarkable resilience, and develops a group of marvelous friendships along the way. Each of September’s friends has marvelous powers, but the powers have very specific limits. And the prose sings to us as we watch these adventures unfold, with characters and settings that glisten and glow as they carry us deep into Fairyland.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380375866i/730554.jpg" width="500" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>The journey is difficult and dangerous, and September must call on all of her resources and learn as she goes. <br><br><i>”Remember, they are fast and tall and vicious! Many have perished or, at least, been roundly dumped off and bruised in the attempt to travel by wild bicycle.”</i><br><br>She is a classic smart, tough heroine, stiffening her resolve with every new challenge. <br><br><i>”September yelped in victory and set about hauling several of the log-size sceptres together and lining them up side by side.”</i><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380375866i/730555.jpg" width="500" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>And yes, there is evil afoot - monstrous and well-disguised, very, very resourceful and SNEAKY. The values that September learns and applies are the classic virtues of loyalty, self-reliance and a persistence that wavers but never dies.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380375866i/730556.jpg" width="400" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>It is a wonderful story, and the story teaches as it tells. The drama builds to a tremendous finish, and I was shaking my head in awe at the end. <br><br>There were points in the story where I struggled with some of the layering, and a few of the twists and turns of events. But it is hard for me to imagine a more beautiful overall effect from beginning to end - one in which all of the pieces are seen (in hindsight) to fit perfectly, and every element is in a sensible place.<br><br><b>Thoughts After Reading</b><br><br>So, I loved it. After I finished this beautiful story, I mused a bit on the comparisons with <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/12887497.Silently_and_Very_Fast" title="Silently and Very Fast by Catherynne M. Valente" rel="nofollow noopener">Silently and Very Fast</a>, and the more general theme of what adults can learn from children’s books (and why they would do well to read them).<br><br>First, the comparisons. In my <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/317732890" rel="nofollow noopener"> review of Silently and Very Fast </a>, I discussed questions that are raised when highly adaptable software takes on human ideas and desires. I mention that discussion here because a related set of questions emerges (for me) in this book. The same gifted writer takes a child through a fantasy world, but includes very ‘adult’ evils, trickery, bureaucracy and manipulation. I had some fun thinking about what (I believe) Valente is getting at, in the deeper levels behind the magic show up front.<br><br>The lesson I drew is that kind-hearted determination, intelligence, and perseverance can push through dark and powerful forces, find the points of vulnerability, and engineer a different and better outcome. For me, this was highly reminiscent in theme to the classic tale of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/18131.A_Wrinkle_in_Time__Time___1_" title="A Wrinkle in Time (Time, #1) by Madeleine L'Engle" rel="nofollow noopener">A Wrinkle in Time</a>, which I <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/296219004" rel="nofollow noopener"> discussed here </a>. Two great writers, teaching important lessons in two fanciful tales with extreme depth, for those who take the time to see them. Adults must work much harder at this, because our own layers of bias and cynicism have likely taught us a very different set of ‘virtues’. But we can see much more, if we really look. Children grasp the essential concepts immediately, unburdened by our adult baggage. But they can get caught up in the fantasy, and may miss the deeper meaning.<br><br>For me, Valente does something incredible in both books that I have read. She uses a mystical fantasy to dazzle the reader, but also to provide an alluring passageway to much deeper ideas. She explores the implications of these ideas, in such a charming setting that the lessons come across as we simply process the fantasy. Here, the net effect is that we get a fresh perspective on matters of ethics, philosophy and 'political' action. And we don’t get the dense, formal or emotionally loaded discussions of ‘adult’ treatments. In Silently and Very Fast, Valente conveys similar implications of ‘intelligence’ and ‘consciousness’ in machines and their human companions, and a trove of other deep concepts. And we don’t get a listing of computer algorithms, or a technical discussion of central vs. distributed processing.<br><br>If I read these two works again, I would start with this one per my original plan, and that would be my recommendation for anyone. But for now, I will be moving on to see what other wonders Valente has in store for us. (Just as soon as I clear away some of the TBR pile that has collected around my feet)<br><br><b>Very Highly Recommended</b><br><br><br>* There are reasonable grounds for doubting whether this is really a children’s book at all. I hope to test this idea on my 5th-grader, but he is absorbed in Charlie Bone at the moment.<br><br><br><br></span>
  <a data-text-id="10600558935582908943" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_380425264" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/380425264" />
    <a title="Algernon (Darth Anyan)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4728718-algernon-darth-anyan"><img alt="Algernon (Darth Anyan)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1553101944p2/4728718.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/380425264?book_show_action=true">Jul 30, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Algernon (Darth Anyan)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Algernon (Darth Anyan)" href="/user/show/4728718-algernon-darth-anyan">Algernon (Darth Anyan)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4728718-algernon-darth-anyan?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4728718-algernon-darth-anyan?shelf=2012">2012</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer380425264" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11263355413984384301"><br/>Consider this fair warning: I'm writing a <i> squee </i> review , <br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380385870i/744970.jpg' width='400' alt='wheeee!' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/>as I think Catherynne Valente is the "bee's knees" when it comes to funny, modern, beautifully written fairytales that can appeal to children and adults in equal measure. Compared to <b> The Orphan Tales </b>, the adventures of the girl September in Fairyland are straightforward and easier to follow, without the frequent jumps from one storyteller to another, while maintaining the emotional intensity and the lyrical prose that first attracted m</span>
  <span id="freeText11263355413984384301" style="display:none"><br>Consider this fair warning: I'm writing a <i> squee </i> review , <br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380385870i/744970.jpg" width="400" alt="wheeee!" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>as I think Catherynne Valente is the "bee's knees" when it comes to funny, modern, beautifully written fairytales that can appeal to children and adults in equal measure. Compared to <b> The Orphan Tales </b>, the adventures of the girl September in Fairyland are straightforward and easier to follow, without the frequent jumps from one storyteller to another, while maintaining the emotional intensity and the lyrical prose that first attracted me to the author. Easy doesn't mean "dumbed down" , and the major selling point of the story for me is exactly this : Valente doesn't talk down to kids, she doesn't coddle and she doesn't hide the pain that is, after all, an integral part of childhood and of life in general. September is a clever girl, she loves to learn new words and her best friend in the new world is a Wiverary (a cross between a wyvern and a Library) with an Encyclopaedic knowledge of everything, provided it starts with a letter from A to L.<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380385870i/744971.jpg" width="400" alt="Ell" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br> <i> September read often, and liked it best when words did not pretend to be simple, but put on their full armor and rode out with colors flying. </i> . <br><br>In a nod to older readers, Valente even includes some theory of relativity and some Schroedinger:<br><i> The casket is really quite clever. I received first marks for it. How shall I explain? It is both empty and full until one opens it. For when a box is shut, you cannot tell what it might contain, so you might as well say it contains everything, because, really, it could contain anything, see? But when you open it, you affect what is inside. Observing something changes it, that's a law, nothing to be done. </i><br><br>At 12 years old, September is just the right age to feel the need to leave the safe parental nest and explore new territories. She is practical, self reliant and curious. Part of this comes from her mother, who is a machinist in an airplane factory. In a move that reminded me most of all of Frank L Baum and his Wizard of Oz stories, September (Dorothy) is one day whisked away from Nebraska (Kansas) by a magical wind and relocated to the land of Faerie (Oz) where she has to fight against the evil Marquess (Wizard). Her companions, instead of Scarecrow, Lion and Tinman, are the wiverary Ell, a blue boy named Saturday and Gleam - a sentient paper lantern. I would not like to give the impression the novel is a pastiche of the classic tale. The world is truly original, the creatures September meets beyond my wildest imagination (a volerie of feral bicycles, soap golems, twin NasNas referencing the Plato myth of perfect spheres, Tsukumogami sentient household appliances and many more). The language is modern, self aware and gently mocking established clichees, with the author sometimes commenting on the text in a secret covenant with the audience:<br><br><i> But I am a sly and wicked narrator. If there is a secret to be plumbed for your benefit, Dear Reader, I shall strap on a head-lamp and a pick-ax and have at it. </i><br><br>here are our heroes starting on their quest:<br><i> September tried very hard to look intrepid on her beast's back, and Ell tried a look of grim determination. </i><br><br>How could I not cheer them on and wished them well? The perils of the magical land are real and September doesn't have any 'get out of jail free' card. Her eyes will be opened to a future of struggle and pain, Death itself being just around the corner for the unwary quester.<br><br><i> We all live inside the terrible engine of authority, and it grinds and shrieks, and burns so that no one will say, lines on maps are silly. </i><br><br>The creatures of Faerieland live in a cruel dictatorship, and September will pay a heavy price for discovering that a heart is the most important thing to find at the end of the journey. Valente proposes at the start of the story that children are 'heartless', selfish little brutes always looking out for Number One, demanding constant attention and believing the whole world belongs to them. In this sense, September journey is one out of this selfish shell, learning responsibility, empathy and appreciation of parents and friends. Coming back to the story of Oz, this is also about courage, and friendship, and finding your heart and standing up to tyrants.<br><br>The upcoming new book in this universe looks really promising. I hope it will be about <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ the shadow September had to sacrifice in the river crossing  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> . I was less impressed by the bonus novella : <b> The Girl Who Ruled Fairyland - For A Little While </b> , but it offered a good fleshing out of the Marquess character. One thing I really like is the general presentation of the book - the font, the illustrations, the cover - it makes a great gift that I intend to push on some friends this next Christmas. Pro-tip: after the last page, go back and re-read the Cast of Characters at the beginning: it's a very funny synopsis of the whole story.<br><br>To close my comments, I should mention that all through my lecture I kept humming a tune by Israel Kamakawiwo'ole, very appropriate for how I felt about the book:<br><br><i>I see trees that are green red roses too<br>I watch them bloom for me and you<br>And I think to myself what a wonderful world<br><br>I hear babies cry I watch them grow<br>And they'll learn much more than I'll ever know<br>And I think to myself oh what a wonderful world<br><br>The colors of the rainbow so pretty in the sky<br>Are also on the faces of the people passing by<br>I see friends shaking hands saying how do you do<br>But they're really saying I love you<br><br>And I think to myself oh what a wonderful world </i><br></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>
  <a data-text-id="11263355413984384301" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1567985862" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1567985862" />
    <a title="Mari" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7013001-mari"><img alt="Mari" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1570550600p2/7013001.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1567985862?book_show_action=true">Mar 03, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mari" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mari" href="/user/show/7013001-mari">Mari</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/10859388-the-girl-who-circumnavigated-fairyland-in-a-ship-of-her-own-making">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7013001-mari?shelf=2018">2018</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7013001-mari?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7013001-mari?shelf=2016">2016</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7013001-mari?shelf=2019">2019</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7013001-mari?shelf=favorites-of-all-time">favorites-of-all-time</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7013001-mari?shelf=my-future-kids-will-read-these">my-future-kids-will-read-these</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7013001-mari?shelf=owls-2019">owls-2019</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1567985862" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1096455598968248707"><br/><i>For full feelings on The Fairyland Series, check out my <a href='https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=EYCIZQVGXVk' rel='nofollow noopener'>video review</a>.</i><br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1570549976i/28263628._SY540_.png' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>This book is my favorite book in my favorite series. I'll front load this review with reasons it might not be for you: Valente is known for her dense, flowery writing. It is very descriptive and a lot of the charm is in just-because places, magic and creatures that rely heavily on tropes created by other fairytales. It is also earnest and dispenses little nuggets of wisdom for people who appreciate a good quotable line. It migh</span>
  <span id="freeText1096455598968248707" style="display:none"><br><i>For full feelings on The Fairyland Series, check out my <a href="https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=EYCIZQVGXVk" rel="nofollow noopener">video review</a>.</i><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1570549976i/28263628._SY540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>This book is my favorite book in my favorite series. I'll front load this review with reasons it might not be for you: Valente is known for her dense, flowery writing. It is very descriptive and a lot of the charm is in just-because places, magic and creatures that rely heavily on tropes created by other fairytales. It is also earnest and dispenses little nuggets of wisdom for people who appreciate a good quotable line. It might be cheesy to others who prefer a little more aloofness or vagueness in their messaging. It is also plot light and detail heavy. If you need a little more purpose in your plot, and struggle with things that amble, this will be tricky for you. <br><br>If you are like me, however, and how well something is written plays heavily into your enjoyment of the book, this will be an absolute treat. This book is steeped in imagination and overflowing with imagery. It is sharp and witty-- a love letter to language, turns of phrase, stories, little girls who save worlds, and magic.<br><br>I am also a big fan of coming of age stories and stories that explore grief; this does both wonderfully. It is a little sad, in the way that fairytales can sometimes be and in the way that growing up can often be. When you think about it, fairy lands can be savage, and the idea of popping in and out of a place is brutal, and this story doesn't shy away from that. That said, this story is also hopeful. The plot is simple, I think, and padded out with lots of places and creatures and sometimes silly details, but it's a journey book, so that was okay with me. It's just so thoughtful in all of its pieces and what they say for September's growing-up, from the scrubbing of her courage, to the break from a home that's bleak and gray with the absence of her father, to the growing of her heart, to the losing it again. It takes fairytale tropes and looks them in the eye and then uses those pieces to seemingly explore a place when it is really exploring a person. <br><br>Relatedly, these characters are now some of my favorite ever. They've earned place in my heart through rereading and because of the incredible growth they experience through their journey in the series. This story led by the brave and wonderful September, flanked by some of the best secondary characters in A-Through-L and Saturday and a freaking 112 year old lantern, who may or may not make me cry every single time. (May.) Even the narrator becomes a character as she interjects into September's story, forewarning us and leading us through this story with care. <br><br>I love this story. Have I mentioned that? Just making sure. <br><br>Below are some quick thoughts from my rereads:<br><br>[April 30, 2019] Marking for reread. I wanted something easy and familiar to read in the middle of a month long readathon and this fit the bill. Forever favorite. I was especially taken by Lye's heartbreaking story this time, perhaps especially because I deeply long for a way to wash off my courage and reset my dreams these days. <br><br>[May 2, 2018] Marking for reread. I lost my original review of this, as I mention below, but this is probably the 4th time I read this book and I still love it as much as ever. It was just what I needed to read, too-- something homey and comfortable during a really stressful time.<br><br>[March 3, 2016] Something happened and I lost my previous reviews of this book. Just know that I loved this every bit as much on third read. It's wordy and whimsical and flowery and a bit silly and a lot heartbreaking and I love it.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1096455598968248707" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer9288865006382703441">This book definitely took me a LONG WHILE to get into. It was a 3 star book up until the last few chapters. I loved the imagination and the emphasis on important things like engineering, problem solving, and bravery! <br/>At first I didn't love it because 1) overhyped and 2) the writing.   <span id="freeText9288865006382703441" style="display:none">This book definitely took me a LONG WHILE to get into. It was a 3 star book up until the last few chapters. I loved the imagination and the emphasis on important things like engineering, problem solving, and bravery! <br />At first I didn't love it because 1) overhyped and 2) the writing. It felt really pretentious at first but once I got used to it and kind of accepted it in an Alice in Wonderland sort of way it was more enjoyable! I was meh on the book as a whole until those last few chapters and then OH MY HEART. <br />September is a wonderful heroine and the world building and writing really is something beautiful after you get used to it.<br />It definitely wasn't one of my all time favorite books ever but it was really enjoyable! I wasn't going to read the rest of the series until those last few chapters, but now I think I'll eventually check them out. :) </span>

<div id="review_2284266207" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

    <a title="~Bookishly" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/28323108-bookishly"><img alt="~Bookishly" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1605967142p2/28323108.jpg" /></a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="~Bookishly" class="user" itemprop="url" name="~Bookishly" href="/user/show/28323108-bookishly">~Bookishly</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781780339818" href="/book/show/17172391-the-girl-who-circumnavigated-fairyland-in-a-ship-of-her-own-making">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/28323108-bookishly?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/28323108-bookishly?shelf=strong-female-protagonist">strong-female-protagonist</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2284266207" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16663735945138482062">I'm actually kind of mad with myself here, as I cannot praise this book as much as I was hoping to. This was a good read, but it wasn't as fantastic as I wanted it to be. The story was sweet, and was comparable to a stick of rock. It hit the right buttons with me in the fairy tale sense, the characters were imaginative, the setting was creative, but that is it. That is where it ends with me. I had no thoughts about it once I'd finished it, and the story hasn't stayed with me, either.<br/>I sound as i</span>
  <span id="freeText16663735945138482062" style="display:none">I'm actually kind of mad with myself here, as I cannot praise this book as much as I was hoping to. This was a good read, but it wasn't as fantastic as I wanted it to be. The story was sweet, and was comparable to a stick of rock. It hit the right buttons with me in the fairy tale sense, the characters were imaginative, the setting was creative, but that is it. That is where it ends with me. I had no thoughts about it once I'd finished it, and the story hasn't stayed with me, either.<br />I sound as if I am totally disappointed with this read, and I assure you this isn't the case.<br />Valente's style of writing is fairly simple, but in this case, it definitely worked. She is clearly a super talented author. The beautiful images at the beginning of each chapter were picturesque, without being overbearlingly so. Now, let me talk about that front cover. Those of you that know me, know that I would buy a book just for the reason of the front cover being beautiful. I mean, isn't that the first thing that attracts one to a book? Anyway, the front cover is gorgeous. It's so authentic, and it has our female protagonist with a key, and a dragon with a chain and padlock wrapped around it, that seemingly needs rescuing. Who needs a man in this situation, hey?<br />The majority of this book was fast paced, but for me, it lagged too much in the middle, and the plot started to get increasingly confusing. Yes, this book is supposed to be a lot of fun and nonsense, but not to the extent of losing the reader altogether. <br />I certainly don't want to put people off reading this book, as others may be able to gain more from it than I did. I am definitely happy I read it, and I'm hoping to appreciate the next installment just that little bit more. <br /></span>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer465902200" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer5475949612861950852"><b>To Embrace or Turn Away?</b><br/><br/><i>“It would have been so much easier to stay in that unhappiness. But like September, I had to say yes to a more extraordinary world, no matter how frightening it was…<br/><br/>“I wanted to create a book about saying yes to magic, about seeing a new way of living and embracing it instead of turning away…<br/><br/>“When I was quite little, maybe four or five, my mom woke me up in the middle of the night and told me to put my bathing suit on. We went outside, and laid in lawn chairs under the fu</i></span>
  <span id="freeText5475949612861950852" style="display:none"><b>To Embrace or Turn Away?</b><br><br><i>“It would have been so much easier to stay in that unhappiness. But like September, I had to say yes to a more extraordinary world, no matter how frightening it was…<br><br>“I wanted to create a book about saying yes to magic, about seeing a new way of living and embracing it instead of turning away…<br><br>“When I was quite little, maybe four or five, my mom woke me up in the middle of the night and told me to put my bathing suit on. We went outside, and laid in lawn chairs under the full moon. She made me a cup of juice with an umbrella in it. She said we were going to get a moon tan, and in the morning, she told me my skin looked silver. It was such a magical moment.”</i><br><br>Catherynne M. Valente (from the Questions for the Author)<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380417776i/826653.jpg" width="400" height="300" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>The Girl with an Orange Dress and Lantern</b><br><br>September is an ill-tempered and irascible twelve year old girl who is very tired of her parents’ house (if that’s not too impossible to imagine).<br><br>The Green Wind offers her the chance to ride upon the Leopard of Little Breezes and be delivered to the Perverse and Perilous Sea that borders on Fairyland. She must then make her own way through that part of Fairyland called Pandemonium.<br><br><i>“Oh, yes,”</i> responds September (if that’s not too impossible to imagine).<br><br>September embarks on her journey in an orange dress:<br><br><i> “She liked anything orange: leaves; some moons; marigolds; chrysanthemums; cheese; pumpkin, both in pie and out; orange juice; marmalade. Orange is bright and demanding. You can’t ignore orange things.”</i><br> <br>You could say the same about September: she’s bright and demanding, and you can’t ignore her.<br><br><b>The Perverse and the Perilous</b><br><br>Like Alice, and as promised by the Green Wind, September encounters the Perverse and the Perilous, without the comfort of her parents. <br><br>She has to journey inwards, into the darkness, into the black, into the subconscious world, where allegorically she confronts the challenges of puberty that await any adolescent (equipped with an orange lantern, of course, but hamstrung by a missing shoe). <br><br>She wishes and wills her way through Fairyland, in a ship of her own making (if that’s not too impossible to imagine), and eventually arrives back home where she awakes in her armchair just as her mother returns from work.<br><br><b>The Every Little Thing That Only Children Can See</b><br><br>Fortunately, September’s mother, like all busy mothers, <i> “cannot see every little thing”</i> and remains oblivious to the adventure her daughter has just undertaken. <br><br>Because September has managed so well herself, all her mother has to do is smile and bundle her off to bed, <i>“snug and whole and warm.”</i><br><br><b>A Note and a Nice Glass of Milk for the Author</b><br><br>Valente spins her magic tale with beautiful pacing, and a love of colours and sounds and words and worlds, both congruous and incongruent.<br><br>It’s a tale that will appeal to 12 year olds, parents of 12 year olds, and anybody else who hasn’t forgotten what it was like to be 12 or ill-tempered and irascible.<br></span>

<div id="review_242565818" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/242565818" />
    <a title=" Danielle The Book Huntress (Back to the Books)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books"><img alt=" Danielle The Book Huntress (Back to the Books)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1403239075p2/1570669.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/242565818?book_show_action=true">Dec 03, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title=" Danielle The Book Huntress (Back to the Books)" class="user" itemprop="url" name=" Danielle The Book Huntress (Back to the Books)" href="/user/show/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books"> Danielle The Book Huntress (Back to the Books)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audio CD 9781441877611" href="/book/show/8474242-the-girl-who-circumnavigated-fairyland-in-a-ship-of-her-own-making">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">fans of mythopoeic fantasy</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books?shelf=faerie">faerie</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books?shelf=library-checkout">library-checkout</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books?shelf=middle-grade-juvenile">middle-grade-juvenile</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books?shelf=all-things-autumn-challenge">all-things-autumn-challenge</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books?shelf=favorite-or-autobuy-author">favorite-or-autobuy-author</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books?shelf=alternate-dimension-or-world">alternate-dimension-or-world</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books?shelf=audiobook">audiobook</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books?shelf=dragon">dragon</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books?shelf=early-to-mid-twentieth-century">early-to-mid-twentieth-century</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer242565818" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17164092345703768477">Reading Catherynne M. Valente is a unique experience. Her writing is full of magic and imagination. It doesn't always make 'sense', but it feels right. The child in me who never grew up, who loves fairy tales, lands of magic, mythical creatures, and folklore, ate up this story like the most scrumptious dessert. I listened to this on audio, and at first, I wasn't sure how well it would work. There are a lot of concepts, and they don't tie together in a straightforward fashion at first glance. If </span>
  <span id="freeText17164092345703768477" style="display:none">Reading Catherynne M. Valente is a unique experience. Her writing is full of magic and imagination. It doesn't always make 'sense', but it feels right. The child in me who never grew up, who loves fairy tales, lands of magic, mythical creatures, and folklore, ate up this story like the most scrumptious dessert. I listened to this on audio, and at first, I wasn't sure how well it would work. There are a lot of concepts, and they don't tie together in a straightforward fashion at first glance. If other readers are like me, I'd encourage you not to give up on it if it doesn't catch you right away on first listen. Initially, I felt that Ms. Valente didn't quite feel comfortable reading her story. However, that changed, and she seemed to get into the flow of it, using different voices, timbres, and cadences for the various characters. I could feel how much she loved this story she had written, and the characters within.<br /><br />This novel is one that both kids and grown-ups with a love of fantasy and make-believe tales would love. It's a story of a young girl who is very, very brave, strong-minded, determined, but with a very big heart for a kid (who are considered to be mostly heartless, according to the narrator). She goes to Fairyland on a romp, to escape the reality of a mother who works all the time and a father who was shipped off to war. Feeling alone and too different from the other kids she went to school with, she longs for adventure and a place where normal isn't the ideal. That's when she gets swept off to Fairyland and becomes a champion for this place of magic. And we are along for the journey.<br /><br />At times, I got a bit confused with the narrative, because it's not exactly a linear story. Fairyland isn't a place that always makes sense, and that could make for strange listening when I was focused on driving or getting where I was going. If the reader embraces that this isn't that kind of novel, it makes for a very satisfying reading experience. Just immersing oneself in this marvelous world where anything is possible is gratifying.<br /><br />This book is suitable for a young audience, but there are elements that feel pretty sophisticated, if one is older and catches the subtext. Some younger readers might not get all those references, but that's okay. I think it's fine for them to grasp an understanding of the story at their own level. There is some violence and dark subject matter, but the message of self-sacrifice, determination, friendship, and love are very good elements for kids to experience.<br /><br />At one point, I thought I'd have to take off half a star because of getting lost and things slowing down a bit, but the overall beauty and power of this story requires a five star rating for me. I definitely recommend this book to readers who enjoy mythopoeic/folklore-rich fantasy novels, young and older.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17164092345703768477" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1758211288" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17713655319703501611">Hovering over the 2 stars rating it says 'it was ok'. I really did want to love this book. I really did. This is my kind of story. It's a Middle grade story about fairies and there is lots of good word play and it's a fantasy. I mean this is all my jam. This is what I come back to over and over. I really had to force myself to finish this. I never got into it. I was never pulled in. <br/><br/>I think part of the problem was I was listening to this in my car and the author, Catherynne was reading this on t</span>
  <span id="freeText17713655319703501611" style="display:none">Hovering over the 2 stars rating it says 'it was ok'. I really did want to love this book. I really did. This is my kind of story. It's a Middle grade story about fairies and there is lots of good word play and it's a fantasy. I mean this is all my jam. This is what I come back to over and over. I really had to force myself to finish this. I never got into it. I was never pulled in. <br /><br />I think part of the problem was I was listening to this in my car and the author, Catherynne was reading this on the CD and that was an issue. She is monotone and very boring. I dreaded having to listen to her. I won't listen to her works again. I don't know why, but I dreaded listening to her. I'm sure that had a little to do with it. I wish she would have let someone else record the story, someone like a professional actor to bring life to it. I think it would have been worth at least one more star if the reader was different<br /><br />This story also reminded me quite a lot of the Phantom Tollbooth, which I loved that book by Norton Juster. I got the feeling that was what she was going for. I am so sad I didn't love this story, I can't tell you how excited I was to have a series of fairy stories to look forward too. Someday, I might try reading another one, who knows, but right now, I think I am done with this story. I'm so disappointed. </span>

<div id="review_165317879" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/165317879" />
    <a title="Lisa Vegan" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/83445-lisa-vegan"><img alt="Lisa Vegan" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1243394822p2/83445.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/165317879?book_show_action=true">May 03, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lisa Vegan" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lisa Vegan" href="/user/show/83445-lisa-vegan">Lisa Vegan</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">everybody ages 8 and all the way up</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/83445-lisa-vegan?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/83445-lisa-vegan?shelf=orphaned-and-quasi-orphaned-kids">orphaned-and-quasi-orphaned-kids</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/83445-lisa-vegan?shelf=fairy-folktales">fairy-folktales</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/83445-lisa-vegan?shelf=childrens">childrens</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/83445-lisa-vegan?shelf=readbooks-female-author-or-illust">readbooks-female-author-or-illust</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/83445-lisa-vegan?shelf=z2011">z2011</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/83445-lisa-vegan?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/83445-lisa-vegan?shelf=speculative-fiction">speculative-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/83445-lisa-vegan?shelf=1-also-at-librarything">1-also-at-librarything</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/83445-lisa-vegan?shelf=goodreads-author">goodreads-author</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer165317879" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15217886620367956217">Nothing less than 5 stars for this gem.<br/><br/>It’s really really hard for me to write a review because I was inundated with so much to say about every page, every line.<br/><br/>This is a wonderful and completely ingenious new fairy tale.<br/><br/>I was chortling from page 1 and 2 and... It’s wickedly funny, and unusually smart. There is something brilliant, funny, touching, quotable on nearly every page.<br/><br/>I appreciated the lack of sentimentality and yet the ability to keep me emotionally engaged.<br/><br/>I’d been a tad worried as I</span>
  <span id="freeText15217886620367956217" style="display:none">Nothing less than 5 stars for this gem.<br /><br />It’s really really hard for me to write a review because I was inundated with so much to say about every page, every line.<br /><br />This is a wonderful and completely ingenious new fairy tale.<br /><br />I was chortling from page 1 and 2 and... It’s wickedly funny, and unusually smart. There is something brilliant, funny, touching, quotable on nearly every page.<br /><br />I appreciated the lack of sentimentality and yet the ability to keep me emotionally engaged.<br /><br />I’d been a tad worried as I’ve seen this compared to Alice &amp; Oz and I’m not a big fan of either. But, if anything, this reminded me of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/497118.The_Phantom_Tollbooth" title="The Phantom Tollbooth by Norton Juster" rel="nofollow noopener">The Phantom Tollbooth</a>, a book I adore; and to those other books too but in ways I thoroughly enjoyed.<br /><br />There are fabulous chapter titles and sub-titles that give hints of what’s going to happen. And I loved the cover illustration and each picture that’s at the beginning of every chapter.<br /><br />What to say about this story? I am not even going to try. Just a few little things: I love September; she’s an amazing character. I particularly appreciated her kindheartedness when she had to eat and had to kill a fish in order to do so. I love the many original characters, and particularly got a kick of the everyday normally inanimate objects that here are alive and sentient. There is a fun twist near the end, which perhaps I should have seen coming but which came as a complete surprise to me.<br /><br />Most enjoyable for me is that while with many books in this sub-genre I usually feel that “it was all a dream or fantasy” with this story I believed everything really happened.<br /><br />This screams loudly that this book is destined to be a classic. <br /><br />There are so many quotes I wanted to include because so much of the book is quotable so here’s just one of many, many memorable passages:<br /><br />“It is well known that reading quickens the growth of a heart like nothing else.”<br /><br />This book fits that bill.<br /><br />If I’d been in the right frame of mind, this could have been a two day read for me, but though it took me many days to finish, I don’t mind because there was so much to savor.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15217886620367956217" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('MYr5JVt3NLuGVoBt1kdI5kEiMVNLAlJp5m7UYM02cmWcyJae3mjZojVHCyIhQO+N3TIUPUor5JaLEw4VY9ZZGQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer18218574969797950636">Catherynne M. Valente was born on Cinco de Mayo, 1979 in Seattle, WA, but grew up in in the wheatgrass paradise of Northern California. She graduated from high school at age 15, going on to UC San Diego and Edinburgh University, receiving her B.A. in Classics with an emphasis in Ancient Greek Linguistics. She then drifted away from her M.A. program and into a long residence in the concrete and cam</span>
  <span id="freeText18218574969797950636" style="display:none">Catherynne M. Valente was born on Cinco de Mayo, 1979 in Seattle, WA, but grew up in in the wheatgrass paradise of Northern California. She graduated from high school at age 15, going on to UC San Diego and Edinburgh University, receiving her B.A. in Classics with an emphasis in Ancient Greek Linguistics. She then drifted away from her M.A. program and into a long residence in the concrete and camphor wilds of Japan.<br /><br />She currently lives in Maine with her partner, two dogs, and three cats, having drifted back to America and the mythic frontier of the Midwest.</span>
